Beyond that, he also mixes in a plus-slider,  above-average changeup and average splitter.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Bauer will begin the  season at Double-A to refine his command but should be one of the first  prospects to make their big-league debut in 2012.&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Top 50 Ranking: &lt;/strong&gt;No. 8&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;ETA:&lt;/strong&gt; 2012&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;","url":null,"embed_code":null,"id":2068394,"updatedAt":"2012-03-27T13:13:49-04:00","title":"Arizona Diamondbacks: Trevor Bauer, RHP"}},{"slide":{"photoHasCropExact":true,"image":{"credit":"Jeff Gross/Getty Images","width":630,"url":"http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/395/118764941_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75","height":420},"photoHasCropNorth":false,"externalId":null,"createdAt":"2012-03-27T00:20:33-04:00","description":"&lt;div class=\"slide-description\"&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Position:&lt;/strong&gt; 3B&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Height/Weight:&lt;/strong&gt; 6'1\", 205&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;DOB:&lt;/strong&gt; 4/16/1991&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Bats/Throws:&lt;/strong&gt; R/R&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Drafted/Signed:&lt;/strong&gt; 2009, second round (El Toro HS, Calif.)&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;span style=\"text-decoration: underline;\"&gt;&lt;strong&gt;2011 Stats&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;High-A: &lt;/strong&gt;.298/.349/.487, .190 ISO, 109 wRC+ (583 PA)&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&nbsp;&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Overview:&lt;/strong&gt; Arenado has a flat bat path that can look awkward at first sight.             <img alt="MLB Prospects: Every MLB Team's No. 1 Prospect" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/368/123175566_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" width="630"/>

              Los Angeles Angels: For the second consecutive season, Mike Trout is the Angels' No. 1 prospect

          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            After publishing
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/articles/1115524-mlb-prospects-top-50-mlb-prospects">
             Prospect Pipeline's Top 50
            </a>
            Monday morning, I've been overwhelmed with the amount of positive feedback that I have received. As one commenter noted, I wasn't concerned with representing every teamwhich is absolutely true. Considering my goal is to assemble a sincere and justifiable Top 50, the last thing I would do is compromise the article's integrity by catering to every single team.
           </p>
           <p>
            So now, since not every fanbase had the opportunity to read about its top prospect on Monday, I have put together scouting reports on every team's No. 1 prospect.
           </p>
           <p>
            For those wondering about the criteria for these players' selections, please refer to the
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/articles/1115524-mlb-prospects-top-50-mlb-prospects" target="_blank">
             introduction of the Top 50
            </a>
            .
           </p>
           <p>
            Now, I fully understand that some of my rankings will generate  criticismand I welcome it. Given my background as a player, coach and  scout, I may view players in a much different light than others. While I  love players with flashy tools, I am not blinded by them. I dont just  look at stats; I scrutinize a hitters swing as much as I do a pitchers  mechanics. What Im trying to say is, Im highly critical.
           </p>
           <p>
            My  Top 50 has been an enormous undertaking to which I have dedicated an  obscene amount of time. Therefore, I want to hear from you, the  readers. Please feel free to contact me with any questions, comments or  criticism. You may share your thoughts in the comments section of this  article, email me at
            <a href="mailto:mrosenbaum@bleacherreport.com">
             mrosenbaum@bleacherreport.com
            </a>
            or reach out to me on Twitter (
            <a href="http://twitter.com/goldensombrero">
             @GoldenSombrero
            </a>
            ).
           </p>
          </div>
          <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--next" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Begin Slideshow">
           Begin Slideshow
           <span class="aquo">
            
           </span>
          </a>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             New York Yankees: Manny Banuelos, LHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="New York Yankees: Manny Banuelos, LHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/369/140779569_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Nick Laham/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             LHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             5'11", 155
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             3/13/1991
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             L/L
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2008, Mexico
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A:
             </strong>
             95.1 IP, 3.59 ERA, 4.01 FIP, 8.87 K/9, 4.91 BB/9, 0.66 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Triple-A:
             </strong>
             34.1 IP, 4.19 ERA, 3.90 FIP, 8.13 K/9, 4.98 BB/9, 0.52 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             As a 20-year-old, Banuelos struggled with his command at both Double  and Triple-A in 2011. The left-hander possesses a swing-and-miss  arsenal of three plus pitches that hes still learning to command. His  fastball sits in the low 90s with more in the tank, and, as of now, his  truest out pitch is a changeup with considerable fade.
            </p>
            <p>
             Hes small  in stature but has broad shoulders to go along with a quick arm. He  repeats his mechanics well, so theres plenty of reason to believe his  command will improve. Pitching to more contact will help Banuelos  minimize his pitch counts and in turn allow him to log more efficient  innings in 2012.
            </p>
            <p>
             Except to see the young left-hander make a midsummer debut in the Bronx.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 28
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2012
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Boston Red Sox: Xander Bogaerts, SS
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:350px">
            <img alt="Boston Red Sox: Xander Bogaerts, SS" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/370/xander_original_display_image_crop_north.png?w=350&amp;h=382&amp;q=75" height="382" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="350"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             SS
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'3", 175
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             10/1/1992
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2009, Aruba
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Single-A:
             </strong>
             .260/.324/.509, .249 ISO, 120 wRC+ (296 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Bogaerts put his name on the map with a .314/.396/.423 professional  debut in 2010 and followed it by blasting 16 home runs in 72 games in  2011. Only 19 years old, his smooth swing and plus power allow him to  drive the ball to all fields with backspin carry. As he faces more  advanced pitching, however, hell be forced to become more selective,  especially with quality off-speed pitches.
            </p>
            <p>
             While he has soft  hands and a plus arm at shortstop, Bogaerts lacks the quickness needed  to remain there. Considering his other tools, he could either end up in  right field or at third baselikely the latter.
            </p>
            <p>
             He may hit a few speed bumps this season at High-A, but thats often the case with elite power-hitting prospects.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 39
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2015
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Tampa Bay Rays: Matt Moore, LHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Tampa Bay Rays: Matt Moore, LHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/371/127992042_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              J. Meric/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             LHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'2", 205
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             6/18/1989
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             L/L
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2007, eighth round (Moriarty HS, N.M.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A:
             </strong>
             102.1 IP, 2.20 ERA, 2.62 FIP, 11.52 K/9, 2.46 BB/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Triple-A:
             </strong>
             52.2 IP, 1.37 ERA, 2.02 FIP, 13.50 K/9, 3.08 BB/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/mlb">
               MLB
              </a>
              :
             </strong>
             9.1 IP, 2.89 ERA, 2.17 FIP, 1.85 xFIP, 14.46 K/9, 2.89 BB/9
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             After  striking out 700 hitters in 497 minor league innings, Moore offered a  glimpse of his potential at the end of the 2011 season when he fanned 11  in his first major league start (against the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/new-york-yankees">
              New York Yankees
             </a>
             , no less) and followed it up by two-hitting the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/texas-rangers">
              Rangers
             </a>
             over seven  innings in Game 1 of the ALDS.
            </p>
            <p>
             The left-hander features the  easiest 94-98 mph fastball Ive ever seen, a plus-plus wipeout curve and  a plus changeup. He has the arsenal and makeup to be an immediate ace,  which is exactly why the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/tampa-bay-rays">
              Rays
             </a>
             locked him up this offseason with a  five-year, $14 million contract with the potential for an additional $26  million between 2017-2019.
            </p>
            <p>
             Although he wont head the young and  talented Rays rotation in 2011, Moore is poised to dominate in his  first full big-league season and should immediately insert his name into  Cy Young contention.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 1
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2011
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Toronto Blue Jays: Travis d'Arnaud, C
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Toronto Blue Jays: Travis d'Arnaud, C" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/372/140656193_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jonathan Ferrey/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             C
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'2", 195
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             2/10/1989
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2007, first round (Lakewood HS, Calif.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A:
             </strong>
             .311/.371/.542, .231 ISO, 150 wRC+ (466 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Travis dArnaud garnered Eastern League MVP honors in 2011 after  posting a .913 OPS at Double-A. His bat has enough pop to be a  middle-of-the-order presence, with the potential to hit 20-plus home  runs while consistently hitting around .280. He could even flirt with a  .300 average with improved plate discipline. He has quick wrists and a  direct bat path that generate power to all fields, and he has already  shown an ability to hit quality off-speed pitches.
            </p>
            <p>
             Although his  defense leaves something to be desired, hes surprisingly athletic  behind the plate with an above-average arm. Still, hes light years  ahead of J.P. Arencibia defensively.
            </p>
            <p>
             Unfortunately, Arencibia,  who will retain a tenuous grasp on the position headed into the 2012  season, currently blocks dArnaud in
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/toronto-blue-jays">
              Toronto
             </a>
             . Therefore, only a trade or  injury to the incumbent backstop will open the door for dArnaud before  an imminent September call-up.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 17
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2012
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Baltimore Orioles: Manny Machado, SS
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Baltimore Orioles: Manny Machado, SS" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/373/140287609_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              J. Meric/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             SS
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'3", 185
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             7/6/1992
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2010, first round (Brito HS, Fla.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Single-A:
             </strong>
             .276/.376/.483, .207 ISO, 131 wRC+ (170 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              High-A:
             </strong>
             .245/.308/.384, .139 ISO, 95 wRC+ (260 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Machado was impressive in his first full professional season despite  suffering a dislocated kneecap and subsequently missing a month. His  6'3", 185-pound frame is extremely projectable; whether its at  shortstop or third base is the only question.
            </p>
            <p>
             He has the actions  to remain at shortstop for the time being, but his physical  development will ultimately dictate his position. He has a plus arm from  the left side as well as average range, so expect Machado to be  projected at both positions over the course of his minor league career.  His plus bat speed suggests potential for plus power, and he has already  shown an impressive feel for the strike zone.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 7
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2014
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Detroit Tigers: Jacob Turner, RHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Detroit Tigers: Jacob Turner, RHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/374/120114967_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Dave Reginek/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             RHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'5", 210
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             5/21/1991
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2009, first round (Westminster Christian Academy HS, Mo.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A:
             </strong>
             113.2 IP, 3.48 ERA, 3.68 FIP, 7.13 K/9, 2.53 BB/9, 0.71 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Triple-A:
             </strong>
             17.1 IP, 3.12 ERA, 2.16 FIP, 10.38 K/9, 1.56 BB/9, 0.52 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              MLB:
             </strong>
             12.2 IP, 8.53 ERA, 6.03 FIP, 4.73 xFIP, 5.68 K/9, 2.84 BB/9, 2.13 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             The ninth overall selection in the 2009 draft, Turner made three starts  for the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/detroit-tigers">
              Tigers
             </a>
             in 2011 as a 20-year-old. Although the results could  have been better, the right-handers stuff was impressive, as was his  overall polish.
            </p>
            <p>
             Turners 6'5" frame allows him to pound the zone  with a heavy, sinking fastball that registers in the low 90s. He  struggles at times with the command of his curveball, but its still a  big-time hammer. Turners changeup is only an average offering as of  now, but he does throw it with fastball-like arm speed.
            </p>
            <p>
             He  probably wont be a strikeout pitcher in the major leagues, but he has  enough movement and deception to induce plenty of weak contact. It  appeared as though Turner would contend for the final spot in the  Tigers' rotation, but he has been shut down for the time being after  experiencing discomfort in his shoulder.
            </p>
            <p>
             He will start the season in Triple-A but should be back in the major leagues before we know it.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 26
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2011
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Chicago White Sox: Addison Reed, RHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Chicago White Sox: Addison Reed, RHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/375/123729065_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Leon Halip/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             RHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'4", 215
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             12/27/1988
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             L/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2010, third round (San Diego State)
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Single-A:
             </strong>
             8 IP, 1.13 ERA, 12.38 K/9, 1.13 BB/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              High-A:
             </strong>
             28.1 IP, 1 SV, 1.59 ERA, 1.54 FIP, 12.39 K/9, 1.27 BB/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A:
             </strong>
             20.2 IP, 2 SV, 0.87 ERA, 1.02 FIP, 14.37 K/9, 2.61 BB/9
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Triple-A:
             </strong>
             21.1 IP, 2 SV, 1.27 ERA, 2.22 FIP, 11.81 K/9, 1.27 BB/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              MLB:
             </strong>
             7.1 IP, 3.68 ERA, 1.93 FIP, 1.70 xFIP, 14.73 K/9, 1.23 BB/9
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Reed, who was drafted in the third round of the 2010 draft out of San  Diego State, has an electric arm with a legitimate out pitch. A closer in college, the 6'4", 215-pounder breezed through the  minors in 2011.
            </p>
            <p>
             He began the year at Low-A Kannapolis and  finished the season in the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/chicago-white-sox">
              White Sox
             </a>
             bullpen. In his 78.1 innings across  four minor league levels last season, Reed posted a 1.26 ERA and 111/14  K/BB ratio.
            </p>
            <p>
             His fastball and slider combination from a  three-quarter arm slot is what one looks for in a closerand he  possesses above-average command of both pitches. He has a changeup,  though he will likely keep it on the back burner given the effectiveness  of his two primary pitches.
            </p>
            <p>
             In a year where the White Sox will  almost assuredly not compete for a division title, I expect Reed to receive the bulk of the save opportunities in 2012. Although Matt Thornton will probably be named the team's closer as big-league camp winds down, Reed has been groomed to close games since college. He has the stuff and experience to be a front-line closer by the end of the 2012 season.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             N/A
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2011
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Cleveland Indians: Francisco Lindor, SS
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:340px">
            <img alt="Cleveland Indians: Francisco Lindor, SS" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/376/FranciscoLindor_display_image_display_image_crop_340x234_crop_north.jpg?w=340&amp;h=234&amp;q=75" height="234" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="340"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             SS
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             5'11", 175
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             11/14/1993
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             S/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2011, first round (Monteverde Academy, Fla.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Low-A:
             </strong>
             .316/.350/.316 (20 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             One of the most promising young shortstops in the game, Lindor will be  on the fast track to the major leagues once the 2012 season is under way.  The best defensive shortstop out of the 2011 draft, he has drawn rave  reviews for his athleticism and fluidity at short. The combination of  his excellent range and plus arm has the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/cleveland-indians">
              Indians
             </a>
             convinced that Lindor  will be able to stick at shortstop for a long, long time.
            </p>
            <p>
             A  switch-hitter, Lindors offensive value will come from his ability to  hit for a solid average and hopefully get on base at a decent clip.  Hell never hit for much power, but he has enough pop to produce 20-plus  doubles. Despite being just a slightly above-average runner, Lindor  projects to steal 20 bases annually due to his instincts and high  baseball IQ.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 29
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2014
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Kansas City Royals: Wil Myers, OF
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Kansas City Royals: Wil Myers, OF" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/377/118760626_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Christian Petersen/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             OF
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'3", 205
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             12/10/1990
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2009, third round (Wesleyan Academy, N.C.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A:
             </strong>
             .254/.353/.393, 9 SB, .138 ISO, 104 wRC+ (416 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             A lot of writers penalized Myers for his lack of power in 2011, which  stemmed from a knee injury and subsequent infection that limited his  ability to drive through the baseball. However, his .360/.481/.674 slash  line in the Arizona Fall League indicates that he has regained his  power.
            </p>
            <p>
             Since entering the minor leagues in 2009, Myers has  absolutely raked at every levelexcluding his 2011 campaign. He has  quick wrists and outstanding bat control that allow him to effortlessly  drive the ball to right field. By the time he makes his debut, Myers  should have 20-plus home run potential and the ability to be a .310-.320  hitter.
            </p>
            <p>
             His plate discipline is advanced beyond his yearslike  teammate Eric Hosmerand hes comfortable hitting in any count. Hell be  nothing more than an average corner outfielder, although the plus arm  that made him an elite catching prospect plays best in right. Now fully  healthy, Myers should light up Double-A pitching and force his way to  Kauffman Stadium sometime this season.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 19
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2012
            </p>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Minnesota Twins: Miguel Sano, 3B
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:254px">
            <img alt="Minnesota Twins: Miguel Sano, 3B " data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/378/miguel_sano_twins_prospect_crop_north.jpg?w=254&amp;h=350&amp;q=75" height="350" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="254"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             3B
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'3", 195
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             5/11/1993
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2009, Dominican Republic
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Rookie:
             </strong>
             .292/.352/.637, .345 ISO, 151 wRC+ (293 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Outside of Bryce Harper, Sano is the best power-hitting prospect in  baseball. He has the ideal combination of quick wrists and explosive  weight transfer that allows him to effortlessly jump the yard to all  fields. If his plate discipline continues to improve, Sano, who turns 19  in May, could hit for a decent average down the road.
            </p>
            <p>
             He can be a  wreck on defense at times, mostly in his actions to and through the  baseball, which suggests an eventual transition to first base. For now  the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/minnesota-twins">
              Twins
             </a>
             will move forward with Sano as their third baseman of the  future.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 16
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2014
            </p>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Texas Rangers: Jurickson Profar, SS
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:480px">
            <img alt="Texas Rangers: Jurickson Profar, SS" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/379/Profar_Rangers_crop_north.jpg?w=480&amp;h=270&amp;q=75" height="270" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="480"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             SS
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             5'11", 165
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             2/20/1993
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             S/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2010, Curacao
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Single-A:
             </strong>
             .286/.390/.493, 23 SB, .207 ISO, 143 wRC+ (516 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Theres a whole lot to like about the 19-year-old Profar, who is the  unanimous top infield prospect in all of baseball. He possesses an  above-average bat from both sides of the plate thats highlighted by an  advanced knowledge of the strike zone. He has surprising strength for  his size that, when bundled with his quick wrists, could yield 15-25  home run potential.
            </p>
            <p>
             Profar also made strides as a base stealer in  2011his first full seasonbut his speed is only above average. Beyond  his obvious offensive potential, Profar is a stud at shortstop. He is a  plus defender with excellent range and soft hands and also possesses a  plus arm that will allow him to remain at the position.
            </p>
            <p>
             Due to  the Rangers current middle infield combo of Elvis Andrus and Ian  Kinsler, theres a chance Profar begins his major league career at  second base. But that will only be temporary, as he is  undoubtedly the teams shortstop of the future.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 5
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2014
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Seattle Mariners: Jesus Montero, C/DH
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Seattle Mariners: Jesus Montero, C/DH" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/380/140952522_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Rob Tringali/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             C/DH
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'4", 225
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             11/28/1989
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2006, Venezuela
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Triple-A (Yankees):
             </strong>
             .288/.348/.467, .179 ISO, 120 wRC+ (504 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              MLB (Yankees):
             </strong>
             .328/.406/.590 (69 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Montero flashed his offensive potential in his late-season call-up with  the Yankees in 2011. Now, after an offseason trade to Seattle,  Monteros path to consistent at-bats is clear as he embarks on his first  big-league campaign.
            </p>
            <p>
             He possesses a middle-of-the-order bat with  exceptional power to all fields, and his ability to hit for average  should make him the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/seattle-mariners">
              Mariners
             </a>
              top hitter in 2012. His swing is compact,  and he takes a direct path to the ball, so expect plenty of  opposite-field extra-base hits too.
            </p>
            <p>
             His future as a catcher has  been heavily scrutinized due to his poor receiving skills and slow  release, but it appears that the Mariners will at least give him a  chance this season. In the long term, though, Monteros bat seems  destined for a 1B/DH role.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 12
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2011
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Los Angeles Angels: Mike Trout, OF
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Los Angeles Angels: Mike Trout, OF" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/381/140185943_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jamie Squire/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             OF
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'1", 200
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             8/7/1991
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2009, first round (Millville HS, N.J.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A:
             </strong>
             .326/.414/.544, 33 SB, .218 ISO, 160 wRC+ (412 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              MLB:
             </strong>
             .220/.281/.390, .171 ISO, 89 wRC+ (135 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Like Harper, Trout has all the tools to be a major league superstar. He  possesses game-changing speed that grades out as an 80 and plays just  as well in the outfield as he does on the base paths.
            </p>
            <p>
             Despite what we  saw in his cup of coffee with the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/los-angeles-angels-of-anaheim">
              Angels
             </a>
             toward the end of the 2011  season, Trout has MLB-ready plate discipline. Thats not to say that he  wont be forced to make adjustments, especially against quality  off-speed offerings from right-handers.
            </p>
            <p>
             He has that rare  power-speed combo to be a legitimate 30/30 when given an everyday job.  His arm is his weakest tool but is above average and suitable for center  field. Considering that the Angels outfield will be overcrowded with  Torii Hunter, Vernon Wells, Peter Bourjos and Bobby Abreu, Trout will  have to wait patiently for his opportunity in 2012. However, its  awfully hard to keep talent like that in the minors.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 3
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2011
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Oakland Athletics: Jarrod Parker, RHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Oakland Athletics: Jarrod Parker, RHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/382/140238612_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Christian Petersen/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             RHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'1", 195
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             11/24/1988
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2007, first round (Norwell HS, Ind.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A:
             </strong>
             130.2 IP, 3.79 ERA, 3.70 FIP, 7.71 K/9, 3.79 BB/9, 0.48 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              MLB:
             </strong>
             5.2 IP, 0.00 ERA, 3.20 FIP, 5.42 xFIP, 1.59 K/9, 1.59 BB/9
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Selected in the first round of the 2007 draft out of Norwell HS in  Indiana, Parker missed the entire 2010 season recovering from Tommy John  surgery. However, he regained his form over the course of the 2011  season and ultimately finished 11-8 with a 3.79 ERA and 7.7 K/9 over 131  innings at Double-A Mobile.
            </p>
            <p>
             Parker has a classic mix of  fastball, breaker and changeup, all of which grade as at least  solid-average offerings. His fastball can touch 97 mph, but he typically  works in the 91-96 mph range with his four-seamer. He throws a heavy  sinker about two ticks off the four-seamer, but it digs well and even  gets some swings-and-misses.
            </p>
            <p>
             Parkers bender is a slider in the  mid-80s with tight break and good shape as well as solid command. His  change is behind, but its going to be an above-average offering for him  and is definitely a pitch that will play in
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/oakland-athletics">
              Oakland
             </a>
             to both sides of  the plate.
            </p>
            <p>
             He will make a few starts at Triple-A to begin the  season, primarily to work on the command of his fastball, but it  shouldnt take him longer than a month to get back to Oakland.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 31
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2012
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Philadelphia Phillies: Trevor May, RHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Philadelphia Phillies: Trevor May, RHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/383/trevor-may-phillies-e1323996796390_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             RHP
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'5", 215
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             9/23/1989
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2008, fourth round (Kelso HS, Wash.)
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              High-A:
             </strong>
             151.1 IP, 3.63 ERA, 2.57 FIP, 12.4 K/9, 4.0 BB/9, 0.50 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             The
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/philadelphia-phillies">
              Phillies'
             </a>
             minor league pitcher of the year in 2011, May led the Florida State League with 208 strikeouts. At 6'5", he is an imposing presence on the mound with two plus pitches. While he can reach back for 98 mph, the right-hander's heavy fastball sits in the mid-90s with late, arm-side run. He's not afraid to challenge hitters up in the zone with it and often uses it as an out pitch.
            </p>
            <p>
             May is one of a select few minor league pitchers who possess the ability to sustain their velocity late into games.
            </p>
            <p>
             His premier off-speed pitch is a plus curveball with serious bite. When May struggles with establishing his arm speed, he has a tendency to spike the pitch. He also features a solid-average changeup that flashes potential at times.
            </p>
            <p>
             The key to his success at more advanced levels will be the development of his changeup, as well as the utilization of a slider he picked up towards the end of the 2011 season. To be efficient with his pitches, he'll have to continue refining his command and making his mechanics more repeatable.
            </p>
            <p>
             Since drafting him in 2008, the Phillies have been extremely cautious in their handling of May. After spending the last three seasons playing for the Phillies' Class-A affiliates, May is clearly ready for a promotion to Double-A. Like so many other prospects, a successful 2012 season will be crucial for his development.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             N/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2012
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Atlanta Braves: Julio Teheran, RHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Atlanta Braves: Julio Teheran, RHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/384/140179367_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Matthew Stockman/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             RHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'2", 175
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             1/27/1991
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2007, Colombia
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Triple-A:
             </strong>
             144.2 IP, 2.55 ERA, 3.06 FIP, 7.59 K/9, 2.99 BB/9, 0.31 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              MLB:
             </strong>
             19.2 IP, 5.03 ERA, 5.87 FIP, 5.21 xFIP, 4.58 K/9, 3.66 BB/9
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Teheran has absolutely nothing left to prove in the minor leagues after  dominating Triple-A hitters in 2011. The right-hander features a  plus-plus fastball in the 93-97 mph range and is aggressive with its  placement, working both sides of the plate and pounding the lower half  of the strike zone.
            </p>
            <p>
             Also in his arsenal is a plus changeup with  excellent fade, as well as a curveball and slider. Both pitches grade as  above-average with potential to be a plus offering in time. He has  showcased improved command of all pitches since 2010 but will inevitably  need more refinement to be as successful at the big-league level.
            </p>
            <p>
             The  dynamic
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/atlanta-braves">
              Braves
             </a>
             rotation is already loaded with impressive young arms,  so Teheran will be forced to begin his 2012 campaign in Triple-A. But  the second there is an injury or the need for a spot start, his phone  will be ringing.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 6
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2012
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             New York Mets: Zack Wheeler, RHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:607px">
            <img alt="New York Mets: Zack Wheeler, RHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/385/Wheeler_TCSP_TC_SPT_SL_METS3_t607_crop_north.jpg?w=607&amp;h=407&amp;q=75" height="407" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="607"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             RHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'4", 185
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             5/30/1990
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2009, first round (East Paulding HS, Ga.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              High-A (
              <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/san-francisco-giants">
               Giants
              </a>
              ):
             </strong>
             88 IP, 3.99 ERA, 3.75 FIP, 10.02 K/9, 4.81 BB/9, 0.72 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              High-A (
              <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/new-york-mets">
               Mets
              </a>
              ):
             </strong>
             27 IP, 2.00 ERA, 1.68 FIP, 10.33 K/9, 1.67 BB/9
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             It must have been hard for San Francisco to part ways with Wheeler,  whom they traded to the Mets in exchange for Carlos Beltran surrounding  the 2011 trade deadline. One of my favorite right-handed prospects in  baseball, Wheeler has a 6'4" frame, fast arm and repeatable mechanics.  When I watch him throw, I see a future ace.
            </p>
            <p>
             His fastball runs as  high as 97, though he usually sits low to mid 90s with late life. His  curveball is a sharp downer that jelly-legs right-handed hitters, and he  also throws a solid changeup that should develop by the time he reaches  the major leagues.
            </p>
            <p>
             While his command still needs some  refinement, Im eager to see how he handles the jump to Double-A to  begin the 2012 season. At this time next year, I have a feeling that I  may be writing about Wheeler as a top-10 prospect.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 20
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2013
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Miami Marlins: Christian Yelich, OF
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:400px">
            <img alt="Miami Marlins: Christian Yelich, OF" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/386/yelich_crop_north.jpg?w=400&amp;h=225&amp;q=75" height="225" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="400"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             OF
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'4", 189
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             12/5/1991
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             L/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2010, first round (Westlake HS, Calif.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Single-A:
             </strong>
             .312/.388/.484, 32 SB, .171 ISO, 146 wRC+ (521 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Still just 20 years old, Yelichs hit tool already grades out as a plus  and has room to grow with improvement in his plate discipline. His  swing is incredibly smooth and fluid, which allows him to attack pitches  throughout the entire strike zone.
            </p>
            <p>
             Due to the level plane of  his swing, Yelich will never hit for overwhelming power, but I think  hell have enough to annually belt a quiet 20-30. As of his now, most of  his power is to the pull side, but he should start driving the ball out  the other way with more experience. His easy speed and good instincts  on the bases suggest that Yelich will have 20-20, perhaps even 30-30,  potential in his prime.
            </p>
            <p>
             Although he patrolled center field for  Low-A Greensboro last season, Yelich profiles as a left fielder due to  his fringy arm strength. However, the Marlins will allow him to develop  in center for the time being.
            </p>
            <p>
             Yelich should begin the season at  High-A with a chance to log significant time at Double-A over the second  half of the 2012 season.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 30
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2013
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Washington Nationals: Bryce Harper, OF
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Washington Nationals: Bryce Harper, OF" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/387/118764357_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jeff Gross/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             OF
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'3", 225
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             10/16/1992
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             L/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2010, first round (College of Southern Nevada)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              High-A:
             </strong>
             .318/.423/.554, 19 SB, .236 ISO, 168 wRC+ (305 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A:
             </strong>
             .256/.329/.395, 7 SB, .140 ISO, 103 wRC+ (147 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Scouts have always been reserved to assign an 80-grade to anything  other than speed, let alone multiple tools. So the fact that Harper, 19,  has two tools that grade as suchpower and armspeaks volumes about his  potential. And its not like his other tools lag behindhe possesses  enough speed to swipe 20-plus bases, the ability to hit for average  thanks to a line-to-line approach and the defensive prowess to stick in  center field.
            </p>
            <p>
             Some are irked by his overall cockiness and hard-nosed mentality on the field. But personally, I
             <em>
              love
             </em>
             it
             <em>
              .
             </em>
             Sure, its a bit immature at times, but hell always be the classic hate to play against, love to have on your team player.
            </p>
            <p>
             In  the face of unscrupulous criticism and unparalleled expectations,  Harper has repeatedly thrived at every minor-league stop, and this year  should be no different. Except to see Bryce Harper in the major leagues  at some point in June.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 2
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2012
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Chicago Cubs: Javier Baez, SS
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:358px">
            <img alt="Chicago Cubs: Javier Baez, SS" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/388/javier-baez_crop_358x243_crop_north.jpg?w=358&amp;h=243&amp;q=75" height="243" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="358"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             SS
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'0", 180
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             12/1/1992
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2011, first round (Arlington Country Day School, Fla.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Rookie:
             </strong>
             .333/.333/.500, 2 SB, .167 ISO, 135 wRC+ (12 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Low-A:
             </strong>
             .167/.167/.167 (6 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             The ninth overall pick in the 2011 draft, Baez has insane raw bat speed  with the potential for plus power by the time he reaches the major  leagues. Simply put: Baez swings as hard as humanly possibleevery time.  But thats also what makes him such a promising hitter.
            </p>
            <p>
             His  defense at shortstop is average, though he does have a strong arm. Given  his size and defensive actions, Baez will probably shift to third base  at some point. He has decent speed and good instincts on the base paths  that give him 20/20 potential.
            </p>
            <p>
             Only 19 years old, the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/chicago-cubs">
              Cubs
             </a>
             will send Baez to Low-A Peoria to begin the 2012 season.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 38
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2015
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>
