            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             St. Louis Cardinals: Shelby Miller, RHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="St. Louis Cardinals: Shelby Miller, RHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/389/97781506_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Doug Benc/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             RHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'3", 195
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             10/10/1990
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2009, first round (Brownwood HS, Texas)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              High-A:
             </strong>
             53 IP, 2.89 ERA, 1.82 FIP, 13.75 K/9, 3.40 BB/9, 0.34 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A:
             </strong>
             86.2 IP, 2.70 ERA, 2.73 FIP, 9.24 K/9, 3.43 BB/9, 0.21 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             After only nine starts for High-A Palm Beach, Miller upped his ETA by  dominating at Double-A Springfield. He has an excellent pitchers frame  at 6'3", 195 pounds, and hell only continue to fill out. Miller throws  a heavy 93-97 mph fastball with outstanding arm-side run that generates  a healthy mixture of swings-and-misses and weak contact.
            </p>
            <p>
             To  complement his heater, Miller throws two above-average off-speed pitches:  a sharp, downer curve and fading changeup. He has already shown the  ability to work deep into games while sustaining his velocity and is  built for innings.
            </p>
            <p>
             Miller should begin the 2012 season in  Triple-A, but he seems on schedule to make a midseason debut. Dont be overly concerned with his well-documented off-field issues  last season eitherits not like he had the college experience to get such  behavior out of his system.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 4
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2012
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Milwaukee Brewers: Wily Peralta, RHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Milwaukee Brewers: Wily Peralta, RHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/390/140080923_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Rich Pilling/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             RHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'2", 240
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             5/8/1989
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2005, Dominican Republic
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A:
             </strong>
             119.2 IP, 3.46 ERA, 3.53 FIP, 8.80 K/9, 3.61 BB/9, 0.68 HR/9
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Triple-A:
             </strong>
             31 IP, 2.03 ERA, 1.78 FIP, 11.61 K/9, 3.19 BB/9
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Peralta was signed  out of the Dominican Republic as a toolsy outfielder in 2005. But  after witnessing his raw arm strength, he was  quickly transitioned to the bump. After missing the 2007 season due to Tommy  John surgery, Peralta has progressed steadily since returning.
            </p>
            <p>
             Peralta pounds the strike zone with a four-seam and two-seam fastball  and typically sits in the low to mid 90salthough he is capable of  touching the upper 90s. His best secondary pitch is a hard slider,  which, when kept down in the zone, is a legitimate swing-and-miss  pitch. He also features a changeup that has come along over the years  due to his role as a starter but at the moment probably only grades  out as about a 50.
            </p>
            <p>
             Although some believe he is best suited for a bullpen role, the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/milwaukee-brewers">
              Brewers
             </a>
             have remained steadfast in their development of Peralta as a  starter. Therefore, it will likely take an injury to a member of the  Brewers rotation for Peralta to get his shot. Until then, he'll wait patiently in Triple-A.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             N/R
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2012
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Cincinnati Reds: Devin Mesoraco, C
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Cincinnati Reds: Devin Mesoraco, C" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/398/124785966_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              John Grieshop/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             C
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'1", 225
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             6/19/1988
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2007, first round (Punxsutawney Area HS, Pa.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Triple-A:
             </strong>
             .289/.371/.484, .195 ISO, 132 wRC+ (499 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              MLB:
             </strong>
             .180/.226/.360, .180 ISO, 48 wRC+ (53 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             The departure of Ramon Hernandez and trade of fellow prospect Yasmani  Grandal has opened the door for Mesoraco, who will finally assume  everyday catching duties for the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/cincinnati-reds">
              Reds
             </a>
             in 2012. As he showed in over 18  games in late 2011, he has some serious thump in his bat. As he  adjusts to major league pitching, Mesoraco should also hit for a solid  average.
            </p>
            <p>
             Although hes not a great receiver and will never throw  out runners at anything more than a 30 percent clip, his bat makes him  serviceable. If he can stay healthy, Mesoraco has the bat to be a  .275-.280 hitter with 20-plus home run potential.
            </p>
            <p>
             He should be  the Reds' everyday catcher to open the 2012 season, but don't be surprised  if Ryan Hanigan steals a few starts per week to help ease him in.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 22
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2011
            </p>
           </div>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Houston Astros: Jarred Cosart, RHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Houston Astros: Jarred Cosart, RHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/391/118764485_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jeff Gross/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             RHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'3", 180
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             5/25/1990
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2008, 38th round (League City HS, Texas)
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
               2011 Stats
              </span>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              High-A (PHI):
             </strong>
             108 IP, 3.92 ERA, 4.00 FIP, 6.58 K/9, 3.58 BB/9, 0.58 HR/9
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A (HOU):
             </strong>
             36.1, 4.71 ERA, 4.49 FIP, 5.45 K/9, 3.22 BB/9, 0.99 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Cosart was dealt to the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/houston-astros">
              Houston Astros
             </a>
             at the trade deadline for Hunter Pence
             <strong>
             </strong>
             and immediately became the top pitching prospect  in the organization.
            </p>
            His fast arm generates 94-97 mph fastballs that can flash up to 98 or 99. Cosart's secondary offerings both grade out to at least a 50 in terms of stuff, but he lacks the command to use them in high volume. At this point,  his changeup is a better out pitch than his breaker, though it does have good shape and pace.
            <p>
             Cosart has an wiry frame with  room to add some bulk. His mechanics range from clean to jerky, but he  is athletic and still has time to refine them.
            </p>
            <p>
             As far as his statistics go, 2011 was an up-and-down season for Cosart. He dominated  through the middle of June, got shelled for a month and a half,  was traded and was ultimately rushed into an unsuccessful stint at Double-A.
            </p>
            <p>
             He'll start the 2012 season back in Double-A, where the Astros hope he'll begin to reverse his converging K/9 and BB/9 rates.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             N/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2012
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Pittsburgh Pirates: Jameson Taillon, RHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:480px">
            <img alt="Pittsburgh Pirates: Jameson Taillon, RHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/392/taillon_2012_prospects_crop_north.jpg?w=480&amp;h=270&amp;q=75" height="270" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="480"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             RHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'6", 225
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             11/18/1991
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2010, first round (The Woodlands HS, Texas)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Single-A:
             </strong>
             92.2 IP, 3.98 ERA, 3.37 FIP, 9.42 K/9, 2.14 BB/9, 0.87 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             I may be one of the only people who sees a higher ceiling in Taillon  than now-teammate Gerrit Cole, but I assure you its with good reason.  Despite his dominance in 2010 for UCLA, Cole has only regressed since  thenalthough his stuff remains exceptional.
            </p>
            <p>
             Taillon, on the other  hand, made impressive strides in his first full season, as he  demonstrated improved command of all pitches. His quick arm generates  fastballs that sit in the 93-97 mph range, and he occasionally flirts  with triple digits.
            </p>
            <p>
             A typical power pitcher, the right-hander  complements his heater with a late-breaking, power slider and  knee-buckling curve. He also has a changeup that grades as  solid-average and will be crucial in his development over the next  couple seasons.
            </p>
            <p>
             Taillon should begin the season at High-A as the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/pittsburgh-pirates">
              Pirates
             </a>
             gradually give him a longer leash.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 11
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2014
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Los Angeles Dodgers: Zach Lee, RHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:200px">
            <img alt="Los Angeles Dodgers: Zach Lee, RHP " data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/393/starter_zach_lee4_crop_north.jpg?w=200&amp;h=266&amp;q=75" height="266" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="200"/>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             RHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'4", 190
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             9/13/1991
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2010, first round (McKinney HS, Texas)
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Single-A:
             </strong>
             109 IP, 3.47 ERA, 3.68 FIP, 7.51 K/9, 2.64 BB/9, 0.74 HR/9
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             After selecting Lee with the 28th overall pick in the 2010 draft, the
             <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/los-angeles-dodgers">
              Dodgers
             </a>
             signed him for $5.25 million just before the deadline. Slated to play both football (QB) and baseball for Louisiana State, the signing bonusthe largest in franchise historylured Lee away from his previous commitment.
            </p>
            <p>
             The right-hander's fastball typically sits in the 90-93 mph range to both sides of the plate, and he'll give hitters a different look by mixing in a cutter. For the first time in his young career, Lee threw both a curveball and slider in 2011, with the latter frequently showing the potential to be a plus pitch. His changeup is pretty mediocre, but it could still be an effective pitch down the road.
            </p>
            <p>
             For someone his size, Lee repeats his mechanics well despite throwing across his body. He exudes confidence on the mound while controlling the pace of the game, traits rarely found in high school pitchers.
            </p>
            <p>
             Lee will likely begin the season at High-A, and considering both his polish and maturity on the mound, he should log significant time at Double-A as early as July.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             N/R
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2014
             <strong>
              <br/>
             </strong>
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Arizona Diamondbacks: Trevor Bauer, RHP
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Arizona Diamondbacks: Trevor Bauer, RHP" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/394/140885889_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Rob Tringali/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             RHP
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'1", 175
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             1/17/1991
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2011, first round (UCLA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              High-A:
             </strong>
             9 IP, 3.00 ERA, 2.20 FIP, 17.00 K/9, 4.00 BB/9
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Double-A:
             </strong>
             16.2 IP, 7.56 ERA, 3.44 FIP, 14.04 K/9, 4.32 BB/9, 1.08 HR/9
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Id be shocked if Bauer isnt the first player from the 2011 draft  class to reach the major leagues. Winner of Baseball Americas College  Player of the Year award and USA Baseballs Golden Spikes Award in 2011,  the right-hander is on the fast track after reaching Double-A last  season.
            </p>
            <p>
             Often compared to Tim Lincecum due to similarities in  mechanics, Bauer is more than just that: Hes a student of the game who  employs a ridiculous work ethic.
            </p>
            <p>
             And then theres his stuff.
            </p>
            <p>
             Bauers  torque delivery unleashes 92-97 mph fastballs on unsuspecting hitters,  although his best pitch his plus-plus curveball, which is the filthiest  of all things filthy and will be considered one of the best in baseball  upon his arrival. Beyond that, he also mixes in a plus-slider,  above-average changeup and average splitter.
            </p>
            <p>
             Bauer will begin the  season at Double-A to refine his command but should be one of the first  prospects to make their big-league debut in 2012.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 8
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2012
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Colorado Rockies: Nolan Arenado, 3B
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Colorado Rockies: Nolan Arenado, 3B" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/395/118764941_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jeff Gross/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             3B
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'1", 205
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             4/16/1991
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2009, second round (El Toro HS, Calif.)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              High-A:
             </strong>
             .298/.349/.487, .190 ISO, 109 wRC+ (583 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Arenado has a flat bat path that can look awkward at first sight.  However, hes strong enough that the swing allows him to hit through the  ball and generate backspin. He has average plate discipline that should  improve with further seasoning in either Double- or Triple-A.
            </p>
            <p>
             After  shedding nearly 20 pounds prior to the 2011 season, Arenado showed  significant improvement at third base and shows potential to be a decent  defender. He has always had the arm strength and instincts to handle  the position, but now his athleticism is finally catching up.
            </p>
            <p>
             In  his prime, Arenado should be capable of 40 doubles and 20 home runs as  either a No. 3 or No. 5 hitter, while still hitting for a respectable  average. He has All-Star potential and should be a run-producing machine  upon his arrival in late 2012.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 21
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2012
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-30 cf display-none " data-page="30">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             San Diego Padres: Rymer Liriano, OF
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="San Diego Padres: Rymer Liriano, OF" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/396/140084539_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Rich Pilling/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             OF
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'0", 211
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             6/20/1991
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2007, Dominican Republic
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Single-A:
             </strong>
             .319/.383/.499, 65 SB, .180 ISO, 157 wRC+ (519 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             Rymer Liriano is a young outfielder with tons of upside. He struggled  at High-A to begin the 2011 season and was subsequently demoted to  Single-A, where he garnered Midwest League MVP honors by slashing  .319/.383/.499.
            </p>
            <p>
             He possesses both plus power and speed, as well  as an above-average knowledge of the strike zone. His ability to hit for  a high average is still suspect but shouldnt detract from his overall  game.
            </p>
            <p>
             Lirianos ability to cover ground in center field and his  above-average arm should allow him to stay in center field for the time  being, but his thick build suggests he might get bulky over time and  require a move to right field.
            </p>
            <p>
             Already on the Padres 40-man  roster, hell get another crack at High-A to begin the 2012 season. If  it goes well, Liriano could rise quickly through the Padres system.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 43
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2014
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-31 cf display-none " data-page="31">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             San Francisco Giants: Gary Brown, OF
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="San Francisco Giants: Gary Brown, OF" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/002/068/397/109381507_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Ezra Shaw/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <div class="slide-description">
            <p>
             <strong>
              Position:
             </strong>
             OF
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Height/Weight:
             </strong>
             6'1", 190
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              DOB:
             </strong>
             9/28/1988
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Bats/Throws:
             </strong>
             R/R
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Drafted/Signed:
             </strong>
             2010, first round (Cal State Fullerton)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
              <strong>
               2011 Stats
              </strong>
             </span>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              High-A:
             </strong>
             .336/.407/.519, 53 SB, .182 ISO, 140 wRC+ (638 PA)
            </p>
            <p>
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Overview:
             </strong>
             In his first full season, Brown opened tons of his eyes with his  80-grade speed and ability to make consistent, hard contact. He has a  knack for peppering the gaps with line drives and is an extra-base  threathe had 61 last seasonthe second he stands in the batters box.  He may never hit 14 home runs again, but it really doesnt matter. His  speed has him pegged as the Giants future leadoff hitter.
            </p>
            <p>
             His  speed also makes him an elite defender in center, which compensates for  an average arm. If his first season at Double-A goes swimmingly, Brown  could debut in San Francisco as early as September, although 2013 is a  much safer bet. He is a hard-nosed competitor with the type of  game-changing speed that will be hard to keep in the minors.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Top 50 Ranking:
             </strong>
             No. 24
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              ETA:
             </strong>
             2013
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
